`_foreach_group_tensors_and_prepare(params, grads, state_tensors, maximize, weight_decay, **kwargs)` - Groups and preprocesses tensors\n\n2. **Main callback-based orchestration function**:\n   - `_foreach_optimizer_step(params, grads, step_fn, state_tensors, **kwargs)`\n   - Handles grouping, assertions, maximize, weight decay\n   - Calls `step_fn(device_params, device_grads, device_states, indices, **kwargs)` for optimizer-specific logic\n\n3. **Common utility functions**:\n   - `_get_group_device_dtype()` - Extract device/dtype from grouped tensors\n   - `_validate_foreach_hyperparams()` - Common validation for tensor hyperparameters\n\n### Files to Modify\n\n**Primary**:\n- Create: `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py` with shared logic\n- Update: `/workspace/torch/optim/sgd.py` - Use _foreach_optimizer_step\n- Update: `/workspace/torch/optim/adam.py` - Use _foreach_optimizer_step\n- Update: `/workspace/torch/optim/adamw.py` - Inherits from Adam (automatic)\n\n**Secondary** (to meet \u22653 file requirement + reduce duplication):\n- Update: `/workspace/torch/optim/adagrad.py` - Use shared helpers\n- Update: `/workspace/torch/optim/rmsprop.py` - Use shared helpers\n- Update: `/workspace/torch/optim/radam.py` - Use shared helpers\n- Update: `/workspace/torch/optim/adadelta.py` - Use shared helpers\n\n## Detailed Implementation Plan\n\n### Step 1: Create `torch/optim/_foreach.py`\n\n```python\n# torch/optim/_foreach.py\nfrom typing import Callable, cast, Optional, Union, Any\nimport torch\nfrom torch import Tensor\nfrom .optimizer import (\n    _to_scalar, _get_value, _view_as_real,\n    Optimizer, DeviceDict, DeviceDtypeDict\n)\n\n# Helper functions\ndef _foreach_apply_maximize(\n    device_grads: list[Tensor],\n    maximize: bool\n) -> list[Tensor]:\n    \"\"\"Apply maximize (negate grads) and return modified grads.\"\"\"\n    if maximize:\n        return torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)  # type: ignore[attr-defined]\n    return device_grads\n\ndef _foreach_apply_weight_decay(\n    device_grads: list[Tensor],\n    device_params: list[Tensor],\n    weight_decay: float,\n    maximize: bool,\n    can_reuse_grads: bool = True\n) -> list[Tensor]:\n    \"\"\"\n    Apply weight decay to gradients with memory optimization.\n\n    When maximize has already allocated new memory for device_grads,\n    we can reuse that memory. Otherwise, allocate new memory.\n    \"\"\"\n    if weight_decay == 0:\n        return device_grads\n\n    # Reuse device_grads memory if it was already allocated for maximize\n    if can_reuse_grads and maximize:\n        torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay)  # type: ignore[attr-defined]\n        return device_grads\n    else:\n        return torch._foreach_add(  # type: ignore[attr-defined]\n            device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay\n        )\n\ndef _foreach_optimizer_step(\n    params: list[Tensor],\n    grads: list[Tensor],\n    step_fn: Callable[..., None],\n    state_tensors: dict[str, list[Optional[Tensor]]],\n    has_sparse_grad: bool = False,\n    maximize: bool = False,\n    weight_decay: float = 0.0,\n    lr: Union[float, Tensor] = 1e-3,\n    **kwargs: Any\n) -> None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Shared foreach optimizer step with common preprocessing.\n\n    Args:\n        params: List of parameters to optimize\n        grads: List of gradients\n        step_fn: Callback function that implements optimizer-specific logic\n        state_tensors: Dict mapping state names to lists of state tensors\n        has_sparse_grad: Whether sparse gradients are possible\n        maximize: Whether to maximize loss instead of minimize\n        weight_decay: Weight decay factor\n        lr: Learning rate\n        **kwargs: Additional arguments passed to step_fn\n    \"\"\"\n    if len(params) == 0:\n        return\n\n    lr = _to_scalar(lr)\n\n    # Group all tensors by device and dtype\n    tensors_to_group = [params, grads] + list(state_tensors.values())\n    grouped_tensors = Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype(\n        tensors_to_group,\n        with_indices=True,\n    )\n\n    for grouped_tensors_tuple, indices in grouped_tensors.values():\n        # Extract grouped tensors\n        device_params_ = grouped_tensors_tuple[0]\n        device_grads_ = grouped_tensors_tuple[1]\n        device_params = cast(list[Tensor], device_params_)\n        device_grads = cast(list[Tensor], device_grads_)\n\n        # Extract state tensors\n        device_states = {}\n        for i, (state_name, state_list) in enumerate(state_tensors.items(), start=2):\n            device_states[state_name] = cast(list[Optional[Tensor]], grouped_tensors_tuple[i])\n\n        # Check for sparse gradients in this device group\n        device_has_sparse_grad = has_sparse_grad and any(\n            grad.is_sparse for grad in device_grads\n        )\n\n        # Apply maximize\n        device_grads = _foreach_apply_maximize(device_grads, maximize)\n\n        # Apply weight decay\n        device_grads = _foreach_apply_weight_decay(\n            device_grads, device_params, weight_decay, maximize\n        )\n\n        # Call optimizer-specific step function\n        step_fn(\n            device_params=device_params,\n            device_grads=device_grads,\n            device_states=device_states,\n            device_has_sparse_grad=device_has_sparse_grad,\n            indices=indices,\n            lr=lr,\n            **kwargs\n        )\n```\n\n### Step 2: Refactor SGD's `_multi_tensor_sgd`\n\nReplace the common preprocessing with `_foreach_optimizer_step` while keeping momentum-specific logic.\n\n### Step 3: Refactor Adam's `_multi_tensor_adam`\n\nApply same pattern, keeping Adam-specific logic (step increment, bias correction, AMSGrad).\n\n### Step 4: Update Other Optimizers\n\nIncrementally refactor Adagrad, RMSprop, RAdam to use shared helpers.\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **Callback approach**: Keep optimizer-specific logic in a step_fn callback to avoid forcing all optimizers into the same mold\n2. **Memory efficiency**: Maintain the existing memory-reuse optimization (e.g., reusing device_grads when maximize is applied)\n3. **Gradual refactoring**: Don't require all optimizers to change at once; allow phased migration\n4. **Backward compatibility**: Existing public APIs unchanged; only internal _multi_tensor_* functions refactored\n5. **Type safety**: Use cast() appropriately and preserve existing type hints\n\n## Testing Strategy\n\n1. Run existing optimizer tests: `python -m pytest test/test_optim.py -xvs`\n2. Verify numerical equivalence between old and new implementations\n3. Check that state_dict serialization still works\n4. Ensure hook APIs still fire in correct order\n5. Validate LR scheduler integration\n\n## Success Criteria Verification\n\n- [ ] `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py` created with shared logic\n- [ ] At least 3 optimizer files import from _foreach (SGD, Adam, Adagrad)\n- [ ] Duplicate foreach patterns reduced (code duplications removed)\n- [ ] Original optimizer APIs still work (all tests pass)\n- [ ] No performance regressions\n\n## Critical Files\n\n### To Create:\n- `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py`\n\n### To Modify:\n- `/workspace/torch/optim/sgd.py` (lines 378-471 of _multi_tensor_sgd)\n- `/workspace/torch/optim/adam.py` (lines 544-787 of _multi_tensor_adam)\n- `/workspace/torch/optim/adagrad.py` (lines ~388-495 of _multi_tensor_adagrad)\n\n### Utilities to Import:\nFrom `torch.optim.optimizer`:\n- `_to_scalar`, `_get_value`, `_view_as_real`\n- `Optimizer`, `DeviceDict`, `DeviceDtypeDict`\n\n## Implementation Notes\n\n1. The _foreach_optimizer_step function signature is flexible to accept any state tensors\n2. Each optimizer's step_fn is responsible for its own logic (momentum, exponential moving averages, etc.)\n3. The shared function handles the \"mechanical\" parts: grouping, maximize, weight_decay\n4. Complex dtype handling will need special treatment - may need helper or documented pattern\n5. Sparse gradient handling varies by optimizer - kept in step_fn for now\n\n## Status: READY FOR IMPLEMENTATION\nPlan is complete and ready for execution. User approval requested.\n",

1. WRITE /logs/agent/sessions/plans/lexical-chasing-kahn.md
# Task: Extract Shared Foreach Optimizer Step

## Context
The PyTorch optimizer implementations contain repeated `_multi_tensor_*` patterns across multiple optimizer files (sgd.py, adam.py, adamw.py, adadelta.py, adagrad.py, adamax.py, asgd.py, nadam.py, radam.py, rmsprop.py, rprop.py, _adafactor.py).

These functions have common preprocessing patterns:
1. Check if params is empty
2. Convert lr to scalar using `_to_scalar`
3. Group tensors by device and dtype
4. Apply maximize (negate gradients if maximize=True)
5. Apply weight decay to gradients
6. Handle the grouped tensors with optimizer-specific logic

## Goal
Create a shared module `torch/optim/_foreach.py` that extracts these common patterns to reduce duplication across 11+ optimizer files while maintaining backward compatibility.

## Key Questions to Explore
1. What exact patterns are repeated across _multi_tensor_* functions?
2. What's the best way to abstract the common logic without breaking the optimizer-specific implementations?
3. Are there existing utilities we can reuse (e.g., from optimizer.py)?
4. What testing approach should we use to verify the refactoring doesn't break anything?

## Status: EXPLORING
Will update after analyzing the codebase patterns.

2. WRITE /logs/agent/sessions/plans/lexical-chasing-kahn.md
# Task: Extract Shared Foreach Optimizer Step

## Context
The PyTorch optimizer implementations contain repeated `_multi_tensor_*` patterns across 11+ optimizer files. These functions have common preprocessing patterns that can be extracted to reduce duplication.

## Exploration Results

### Common Patterns Found Across _multi_tensor_* Functions
1. **Empty parameter check**: All return early if `len(params) == 0`
2. **LR scalar conversion**: `lr = _to_scalar(lr)`
3. **Tensor grouping**: `Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype([...], with_indices=True)`
4. **Maximize handling**: `if maximize: device_grads = torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)`
5. **Weight decay**: Memory-optimized addition with reuse of intermediate tensors
6. **Assertions**: `assert not differentiable` and `assert grad_scale is None and found_inf is None`
7. **Complex dtype handling**: `_view_as_real(...)` pattern
8. **CPU step optimization**: Avoid repeated tensor wrapping for CPU-resident state

### Utilities Available for Reuse
From `torch.optim.optimizer`:
- `_to_scalar()` - Convert tensor LR to scalar
- `_get_value()` - Extract Python value from tensor
- `_view_as_real()` - Convert complex tensors for processing
- `_get_scalar_dtype()`, `_get_capturable_supported_devices()`
- Type aliases: `DeviceDict`, `DeviceDtypeDict`
- `Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()` - Core grouping utility

### Optimizer-Specific Differences
- **SGD**: Momentum buffer handling, sparse gradient fallback
- **Adam**: Parameter validation, step increment, decoupled weight decay, AMSGrad logic
- **RMSprop**: Complex handling, centered variance, CPU step optimization
- **Adagrad**: Sparse gradient fallback, LR decay per parameter
- Each has distinct bias correction and state update logic that can't be fully abstr
... (truncated)
3. WRITE /workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py
# mypy: allow-untyped-defs
r"""Shared foreach optimizer utilities.

This module contains common preprocessing logic for foreach (_multi_tensor_)
optimizer implementations to reduce code duplication across optimizer files.
"""

from typing import Any, Callable, cast, Optional, Union

import torch
from torch import Tensor

from .optimizer import (
    DeviceDict,
    DeviceDtypeDict,
    Optimizer,
    _to_scalar,
)


__all__ = [
    "apply_maximize",
    "apply_weight_decay",
]


def apply_maximize(
    device_grads: list[Tensor],
    maximize: bool,
) -> list[Tensor]:
    """Apply maximize operation (negate gradients) to gradient list.

    Args:
        device_grads: List of gradients for a specific device/dtype group
        maximize: Whether to maximize loss (requires negating gradients)

    Returns:
        Modified gradient list (negated if maximize=True, otherwise unchanged)
    """
    if maximize:
        return torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)  # type: ignore[attr-defined]
    return device_grads


def apply_weight_decay(
    device_grads: list[Tensor],
    device_params: list[Tensor],
    weight_decay: float,
    maximize: bool,
    can_reuse_grads: bool = True,
) -> list[Tensor]:
    """Apply weight decay to gradients with memory optimization.

    This function optimizes memory usage by reusing the device_grads allocation
    when it has already been allocated for the maximize operation.

    Args:
        device_grads: List of gradients for a specific device/dtype group
        device_params: List of parameters for the same device/dtype group
        weight_decay: Weight decay coefficient
        maximize: Whether maximize has already been applied (and allocated new memory)
        can_reuse_grads: Whether the device_grads memory can be safely reused

    
... (truncated)

        if weight_decay != 0:
            # Reuse the intermediate memory (device_grads) already allocated for maximize
            if maximize:
                torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay)
            else:

7. EDIT /workspace/torch/optim/adam.py
Before
        if maximize:
            device_grads = torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)  # type: ignore[assignment]

        # Update steps
        # If steps are on CPU, foreach will fall back to the slow path, which is a for-loop calling t.add(1) over
        # and over. 1 will then be wrapped into a Tensor over and over again, which is slower than if we just
        # wrapped it once now. The alpha is required to assure we go to the right overload.
        if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and device_state_steps[0].is_cpu:
            torch._foreach_add_(
                device_state_steps, torch.tensor(1.0, device="cpu"), alpha=1.0
            )
        else:
            torch._foreach_add_(device_state_steps, 1)

        if weight_decay != 0:
            if decoupled_weight_decay:
                # Perform stepweight decay
                torch._foreach_mul_(device_params, 1 - lr * weight_decay)
            else:
                # Reuse the intermediate memory (device_grads) already allocated for maximize
                if maximize:
                    torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay)
                else:
                    device_grads = torch._foreach_add(  # type: ignore[assignment]
                        device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay
                    )
After
        device_grads = apply_maximize(device_grads, maximize)  # type: ignore[assignment]

        # and over. 1 will then be wrapped into a Tensor over and over again, which is slower than if we just
        # wrapped it once now. The alpha is required to assure we go to the right overload.
        if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and device_state_steps[0].is_cpu:

#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""Verify the implementation meets all success criteria."""
import os
import re

def check_file_exists(filepath):
    """Check if a file exists."""
    exists = os.path.exists(filepath)
    status = "✓" if exists else "✗"
    print(f"{status} File exists: {filepath}")
    return exists

def check_imports_in_file(filepath, module_name):
    """Check if a file imports from the specified module."""
    with open(filepath, 'r') as f:
        content = f.read()
    imports = re.findall(rf'from \._foreach import|from torch\.optim\._foreach import', content)
    has_import = len(imports) > 0
    status = "✓" if has_import else "✗"
    print(f"{status} {filepath} imports from _foreach: {has_import}")
    return has_import

def count_function_uses(filepath, func_name):
    """Count how many times a function is used in a file."""
    with open(filepath, 'r') as f:
        content = f.read()
    # Don't count the import line
    uses = content.count(f"{func_name}(")
    uses -= content.count(f"from ._foreach import {func_name}")  # Subtract import statement
    return uses

print("=" * 60)
print("IMPLEMENTATION VERIFICATION")
print("=" * 60)

# Check 1: _foreach.py exists
print("\n[1] Checking _foreach.py creation...")
foreach_exists = check_file_exists("torch/optim/_foreach.py")

# Check 2: Check that at least 3 optimizer files import from _foreach
print("\n[2] Checking optimizer imports from _foreach...")
optimizer_files = {
    "torch/optim/sgd.py": "SGD",
    "torch/optim/adam.py": "Adam",
    "torch/optim/adagrad.py": "Adagrad",
    "torch/optim/adamw.py": "AdamW",
}
imported_count = 0
for filepath, name in optimizer_files.items():
    if os.path.exists(filepath):
        if check_imports_in_file(filepath, "._foreach"):
            imported_count += 1

print(f"\n→ Optimizers importing from _foreach: {imported_count}/4")
success_import = imported_count >= 3
print(f"{'✓' if success_import else '✗'} At least 3 optimizers import from _foreach: {success_import}")

# Check 3: Verify functions are used
print("\n[3] Checking function usage...")
for filepath in ["torch/optim/sgd.py", "torch/optim/adam.py", "torch/optim/adagrad.py"]:
    if os.path.exists(filepath):
        maximize_uses = count_function_uses(filepath, "apply_maximize")
        weight_decay_uses = count_function_uses(filepath, "apply_weight_decay")
        print(f"{filepath}:")
        print(f"  - apply_maximize() used: {maximize_uses} times")
        print(f"  - apply_weight_decay() used: {weight_decay_uses} times")

# Check 4: Verify _foreach.py has the required functions
print("\n[4] Checking _foreach.py content...")
with open("torch/optim/_foreach.py", 'r') as f:
    content = f.read()
has_apply_maximize = "def apply_maximize(" in content
has_apply_weight_decay = "def apply_weight_decay(" in content
print(f"{'✓' if has_apply_maximize else '✗'} apply_maximize function defined: {has_apply_maximize}")
print(f"{'✓' if has_apply_weight_decay else '✗'} apply_weight_decay function defined: {has_apply_weight_decay}")

# Summary
print("\n" + "=" * 60)
print("SUCCESS CRITERIA SUMMARY")
print("=" * 60)
criteria = [
    ("_foreach.py exists", foreach_exists),
    ("At least 3 optimizers import from _foreach", success_import),
    ("Both shared functions defined", has_apply_maximize and has_apply_weight_decay),
]
all_passed = all(value for _, value in criteria)
for criterion, passed in criteria:
    status = "✓" if passed else "✗"
    print(f"{status} {criterion}")

print(f"\n{'✅ ALL CRITERIA MET' if all_passed else '❌ SOME CRITERIA FAILED'}")
EOF
